--- Commit Message ---
LU-14535 quota: get all quota info in LFS

This patch adds option "-a" for LFS to get the quota info of
all quota IDs. it iterates quota setting saved in global quota
setting files "quota_master/md-0x0" and "quota_master/dt-0x0"
from QMT and iterates the quota usage info saved in acct quota
files in the backend FS (LDiskFS or ZFS) from QSDs, then merge
the two kinds of quota info at client and print it in the similar
way as "lfs quota -u|-g|-p".

  $lfs quota -a -u /mnt/lustre
  Filesystem /mnt/lustre, Disk usr quotas
  quota_id  kbytes   quota   limit   grace   files quota limit  grace
      root    9684       0       0       -    1019    0     0       -
       bin       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
    daemon       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
       adm       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
        lp       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
      sync       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
  shutdown       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
      halt       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -
      mail       4       0  102400       -       1    0  10240      -

  $lfs quota -a -g /mnt/lustre
  Filesystem /mnt/lustre, Disk grp quotas
  quota_id  kbytes   quota   limit   grace   files quota limit  grace
      root    9684       0       0       -    1019    0      0      -
       bin       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
    daemon       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
       adm       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
        lp       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
      sync       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
  shutdown       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
      halt       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -
      mail       4       0  204800       -       1    0  20480      -

This patch also fixes an deadlock issue in qmt_pool_recalc,
the rw_semaphore "qmt_pool_info.qpi_sarr.osts.op_rw_sem" has been
acquired in qmt_pool_recalc (read mode), but it was acquired once
more in qmt_seed_glbe_all (read mode) and will be stuck if there
is a pending write mode lock acquisition from another thread.

 qsd_reint_qpool D
 Call Trace:
    schedule+0x29/0x70
    rwsem_down_read_failed+0x105/0x1c0
    call_rwsem_down_read_failed+0x18/0x30
    down_read+0x20/0x40
    qmt_seed_glbe_all+0x3a0/0x800 [lquota]
    qmt_site_recalc_cb+0x3c7/0x800 [lquota]
    cfs_hash_for_each_tight+0x11e/0x330
    cfs_hash_for_each+0x10/0x20 [libcfs]
    qmt_pool_recalc+0x9fc/0x1310 [lquota]

 llog_process_th D
 Call Trace:
    schedule+0x29/0x70
    rwsem_down_write_failed+0x215/0x3c0
    call_rwsem_down_write_failed+0x17/0x30
    down_write+0x2d/0x3d
    lu_tgt_pool_remove+0x36/0x1e0 [obdclass]
    qmt_pool_add_rem+0x655/0x920 [lquota]
    qmt_pool_rem+0x10/0x20 [lquota]
    lod_pool_remove_q+0xd6/0x1d0 [lod]
    class_process_config+0x16f2/0x2b20
    class_config_llog_handler+0x839/0x1540
    llog_process_thread+0x913/0x1c10

--- Message (James Simmons, 2021-03-19 14:42:31.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1:

(2 comments)

You can't pass that amount of data back through an ioctl. ioctls in Linux only have a 32K buffer limit per call. The way Lustre normally gets around this is by calling the ioctl over and over again with an incrementing index argument until an error happens. See OBD_IOC_GETDEVICE for example. Another option for dealing with this amount of data is by using Netlink.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-03-20 07:52:53.000000000) ---
Patch Set 1: Code-Review-1

(18 comments)

It isn't quite clear to me how this all works, but a reasonable model to follow is like FIEMAP and readdir.  

Userspace supplies a buffer with a header that describes how many entries fit into it, and the starting/ending range of quota IDs, types, etc. Typically this might be "[0,~0]" to get all records, but maybe allowing a sub-range would be useful. 

 The kernel replies with a filled in buffer that has not more than the requested number of entries, and the count of entries returned.  If multiple types are requested (u,g,p) then they should be in a specific order so that there is a clear way to restart the iteration.

If we think it makes sense to print eg. u=1000, g=1000, p=1000 together because they are likely to be related, then they should be returned together, and the kernel should not put a partial set of records into the buffer if there isn't enough room for all of them. That would make restarting easier, since it would only need the id number to restart. 

If more entries are needed, userspace calls again with the header having the starting range at one more than the last record returned (and the type of the last record plus any later types, if needed).

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2021-03-20 07:53:46.000000000) ---

Hongchao, have you tested this with a patched client and unpatched servers?  Since this is changing the network protocol to add the new ITERQUOTA command, it would be good to check that this doesn't cause any problems for an old server that doesn't understand it, or cause the client to fail badly.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-01-24 00:24:29.000000000) ---
Patch Set 48: Code-Review-1

(40 comments)

I think there is a path forward to get this patch landed with relatively small changes, but some way to allow fixing the "get all quotas first, then call multiple times to print" implementation and the issues with concurrent "lfs quota -a" callers.

The minimal fix is to have a per-caller quota_iter_list structure that is (currently) identified by the "mark" value.  The "mark" usage/implementation could later be changed to be an index value for doing proper iteration of quota types/IDs between calls into the kernel instead of getting all quotas in advance.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-08-28 15:44:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 52:

So the question is what does the output look like? Also what does this interface give us that the standard quota utilities doesn't?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-08-30 00:54:01.000000000) ---
Patch Set 52:

> So the question is what does the output look like?

This is included in the commit message, though I agree it is hidden by the discussion of qmt_pool_recalc deadlock (which I will move to the end).

 > Also what does
 > this interface give us that the standard quota utilities doesn't?

The Linux quota utilities depend on having a block device, which a Lustre client does not have, so they have never worked for Lustre.  This patch is just adding the ability to dump all quotas at the same time, rather than having to list them one-at-a-time.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-09-02 03:55:50.000000000) ---
Patch Set 54:

> Sad we don't support the standard
 > quota tools tho. I need to look into that down the road.

As previously mentioned, the kernel quota tools depend on working with a local block device, and that isn't possible with a network filesystem. There was some discussion on Linux-fsdevel about allowing ioctls on the filesystem root device, which would be OK to support in Lustre so the standard tools also worked.

However, I don't think the kernel quota tools will ever support dumpling info about OST and MDT usage, project quotas, OST pool quotas, etc. so we will need to continue to have Lustre-specific quota interfaces.

this could be introduced by the patch https://review.whamcloud.com/c/fs/lustre-release/+/45098

There is one lock held in cfs_hash_for_each_relax, cfs_hash.hs_lops = cfs_hash_bkt_rw_sem_lops)
The other lock is being tried to acquire in qmt_lvbo_free during freeing the lock by calling cfs_hash_put_locked in cfs_hash_for_each_relax.

Could the issue be more easy to reproduced after applying this patch?

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2023-10-15 11:25:39.000000000) ---
Patch Set 54: -Code-Review

It looks like the hash code may be getting a spinlock, but qmt_lvbo_free() is acquiring the lqe_glbl_data_lock mutex:

 cfs_hash_for_each_relax
 ldlm_cancel_lock_for_export
 cfs_hash_for_each_empty
 ldlm_export_cancel_locks

However, lqe_glbl_data_lock cannot be changed into a spinlock because it is also held in other places which might sleep.

The patch https://review.whamcloud.com/45882 "LU-8130 ldlm: convert ldlm_resource hash to rhashtable" *might* help in this case, but I'm not sure.

--- Message (James Simmons, 2023-10-15 15:10:09.000000000) ---
Patch Set 54:

We would need to port the export_lock_hash to rhashtable which is a new patch.
